That afternoon, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Japan" title="Prime Minister of Japan">Prime Minister</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suzuki_Kantar%C5%8D" title="Suzuki Kantarō">Suzuki Kantarō</a> declared at a press conference that the Potsdam Declaration was no more than a rehash (<i>yakinaoshi</i>) of the <a href="/wiki/1943_Cairo_Declaration" title="1943 Cairo Declaration">Cairo Declaration</a> and that the government intended to ignore it (<i><a href="/wiki/Mokusatsu" title="Mokusatsu">mokusatsu</a></i>, "kill by silence").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The statement was taken by both Japanese and foreign papers as a clear rejection of the declaration. Emperor Hirohito, who was waiting for a Soviet reply to non-committal Japanese peace feelers, made no move to change the government position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBix1996290_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix1996290-103">[103]</a></sup> Japan's willingness to surrender remained conditional on the preservation of the imperial institution; that Japan not be occupied; that the Japanese armed forces be disbanded voluntarily; and that war criminals be prosecuted by Japanese courts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAsada199639_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAsada199639-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>At Potsdam, Truman agreed to a request from <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> that Britain be represented when the atomic bomb was dropped. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_Penney" title="William Penney">William Penney</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Group_Captain" title="Group Captain">Group Captain</a> <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Cheshire" title="Leonard Cheshire">Leonard Cheshire</a> were sent to Tinian, but found that LeMay would not let them accompany the mission. All they could do was send a strongly worded signal back to Wilson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977326.2C_356.2C_370_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977326.2C_356.2C_370-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bombs">Bombs</span></h3>
<p>The Little Boy bomb, except for the uranium payload, was ready at the beginning of May 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoddesonHenriksenMeadeWestfall1993262_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoddesonHenriksenMeadeWestfall1993262-106">[106]</a></sup> The uranium-235 projectile was completed on June 15, and the target insert on July 24.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoddesonHenriksenMeadeWestfall1993265_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoddesonHenriksenMeadeWestfall1993265-107">[107]</a></sup> The target and bomb pre-assemblies (partly assembled bombs without the fissile components) left <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunters_Point_Naval_Shipyard" title="Hunters Point Naval Shipyard">Hunters Point Naval Shipyard</a>, California, on July 16 aboard the <a href="/wiki/Cruiser" title="Cruiser">cruiser</a> <a href="/wiki/USS_Indianapolis_(CA-35)" title="USS Indianapolis (CA-35)">USS <i>Indianapolis</i></a>, and arrived on Tinian on July 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoster-Mullen201230_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoster-Mullen201230-108">[108]</a></sup> The target inserts followed by air on July 30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoddesonHenriksenMeadeWestfall1993265_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoddesonHenriksenMeadeWestfall1993265-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plutonium_core" title="Plutonium core">plutonium core</a>, along with its <a href="/wiki/Polonium" title="Polonium">polonium</a>-<a href="/wiki/Beryllium" title="Beryllium">beryllium</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urchin_(detonator)" title="Urchin (detonator)">urchin initiator</a>, was transported in the custody of Project Alberta courier <a href="/wiki/Raemer_Schreiber" title="Raemer Schreiber">Raemer Schreiber</a> in a magnesium field carrying case designed for the purpose by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Morrison" title="Philip Morrison">Philip Morrison</a>. Magnesium was chosen because it does not act as a <a href="/wiki/Neutron_reflector" title="Neutron reflector">tamper</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoster-Mullen201245_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoster-Mullen201245-109">[109]</a></sup> The core departed from <a href="/wiki/Kirtland_Air_Force_Base" title="Kirtland Air Force Base">Kirtland Army Air Field</a> on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C-54" title="C-54">C-54</a> transport aircraft of the 509th Composite Group's <a href="/wiki/320th_Troop_Carrier_Squadron" title="320th Troop Carrier Squadron">320th Troop Carrier Squadron</a> on July 26, and arrived at North Field July 28. Three Fat Man high-explosive pre-assemblies, designated F31, F32, and F33, were picked up at Kirtland on July 28 by three B-29s, two from the 393d Bombardment Squadron plus one from the 216th Army Air Force Base Unit, and transported to North Field, arriving on August 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECampbell200538.E2.80.9340_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECampbell200538.E2.80.9340-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hiroshima">Hiroshima</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hiroshima_during_World_War_II">Hiroshima during World War II</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:B-29_Enola_Gay_w_Crews.jpg"><img alt='A Silver aircraft with "Enola Gay" and "82" painted on the nose. Seven men stand in front of it. Four are wearing shorts, four are wearing T-shirts, and the only ones with hats have baseball caps. Tibbets is distinctively wearing correct uniform.' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/B-29_Enola_Gay_w_Crews.jpg/220px-B-29_Enola_Gay_w_Crews.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/B-29_Enola_Gay_w_Crews.jpg/330px-B-29_Enola_Gay_w_Crews.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/B-29_Enola_Gay_w_Crews.jpg/440px-B-29_Enola_Gay_w_Crews.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:B-29_Enola_Gay_w_Crews.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i><a href="/wiki/Enola_Gay" title="Enola Gay">Enola Gay</a></i> dropped the "<a href="/wiki/Little_Boy" title="Little Boy">Little Boy</a>" atomic bomb on Hiroshima. In this photograph are five of the aircraft's ground crew with mission commander <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tibbets" title="Paul Tibbets">Paul Tibbets</a> in the center.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the time of its bombing, Hiroshima was a city of both industrial and military significance. A number of military units were located nearby, the most important of which was the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Gensui_(Imperial_Japanese_Army)" title="Gensui (Imperial Japanese Army)">Field Marshal</a> <a href="/wiki/Shunroku_Hata" title="Shunroku Hata">Shunroku Hata</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Second_General_Army_(Japan)" title="Second General Army (Japan)">Second General Army</a>, which commanded the defense of all of southern Japan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiangreco200964.E2.80.9365.2C_163_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiangreco200964.E2.80.9365.2C_163-111">[111]</a></sup> and was located in <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima_Castle" title="Hiroshima Castle">Hiroshima Castle</a>. Hata's command consisted of some 400,000 men, most of whom were on Kyushu where an Allied invasion was correctly anticipated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldsteinDillonWenger199541_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldsteinDillonWenger199541-112">[112]</a></sup> Also present in Hiroshima were the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Fifty-Ninth_Army_(Japan)" title="Fifty-Ninth Army (Japan)">59th Army</a>, the <a href="/wiki/5th_Division_(Imperial_Japanese_Army)" title="5th Division (Imperial Japanese Army)">5th Division</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/224th_Division_(Imperial_Japanese_Army)" title="224th Division (Imperial Japanese Army)">224th Division</a>, a recently formed mobile unit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiangreco200970.2C_163_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiangreco200970.2C_163-113">[113]</a></sup> The city was defended by five batteries of 7-cm and 8-cm (2.8 and 3.1 inch) <a href="/wiki/Anti-aircraft_warfare" title="Anti-aircraft warfare">anti-aircraft guns</a> of the 3rd Anti-Aircraft Division, including units from the 121st and 122nd Anti-Aircraft Regiments and the 22nd and 45th Separate Anti-Aircraft Battalions. In total, an estimated 40,000 Japanese military personnel were stationed in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZalogaNoon201059_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZalogaNoon201059-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hiroshima was a minor supply and logistics base for the Japanese military, but it also had large stockpiles of military supplies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-effects_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-effects-115">[115]</a></sup> The city was also a communications center, a key port for shipping and an assembly area for troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones1985529_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones1985529-76">[76]</a></sup> It was a beehive of war industry, manufacturing parts for planes and boats, for bombs, rifles, and handguns; children were shown how to construct and hurl gasoline bombs and the wheelchair-bound and bedridden were assembling booby traps to be planted in the beaches of Kyushu. A new slogan appeared on the walls of Hiroshima: "FORGET SELF! ALL OUT FOR YOUR COUNTRY!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977224-225_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977224-225-116">[116]</a></sup> It was also the second largest city in Japan after Kyoto that was still undamaged by air raids,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGroves1962316_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGroves1962316-117">[117]</a></sup> due to the fact that it lacked the aircraft manufacturing industry that was the XXI Bomber Command's priority target. On July 3, the Joint Chiefs of Staff placed it off limits to bombers, along with Kokura, Niigata and Kyoto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrank1999263_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrank1999263-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>The center of the city contained several <a href="/wiki/Reinforced_concrete" title="Reinforced concrete">reinforced concrete</a> buildings and lighter structures. Outside the center, the area was congested by a dense collection of small timber-made workshops set among Japanese houses. A few larger industrial plants lay near the outskirts of the city. The houses were constructed of timber with tile roofs, and many of the industrial buildings were also built around timber frames. The city as a whole was highly susceptible to fire damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts197738_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts197738-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>The population of Hiroshima had reached a peak of over 381,000 earlier in the war but prior to the atomic bombing, the population had steadily decreased because of a <a href="/wiki/Evacuations_of_civilians_in_Japan_during_World_War_II" title="Evacuations of civilians in Japan during World War II">systematic evacuation ordered by the Japanese government</a>. At the time of the attack, the population was approximately 340,000–350,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rerf-deaths_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-rerf-deaths-120">[120]</a></sup> Residents wondered why Hiroshima had been spared destruction by firebombing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBodden200720_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBodden200720-121">[121]</a></sup> Some speculated that the city was to be saved for U.S. occupation headquarters, others thought perhaps their relatives in Hawaii and California had petitioned the U.S. government to avoid bombing Hiroshima.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPreston2005262_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPreston2005262-122">[122]</a></sup> More realistic city officials had ordered buildings torn down to create long, straight <a href="/wiki/Firebreak" title="Firebreak">firebreaks</a>, beginning in 1944.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFi.C3.A9v.C3.A9Waley2003330_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFi.C3.A9v.C3.A9Waley2003330-123">[123]</a></sup> Firebreaks continued to be expanded and extended up to the morning of August 6, 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERotter2008267_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERotter2008267-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bombing_of_Hiroshima">Bombing of Hiroshima</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hirgrnd1.jpg"><img alt="A mushroom cloud forming." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="359" data-file-width="277" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/13/Hirgrnd1.jpg/170px-Hirgrnd1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/13/Hirgrnd1.jpg/255px-Hirgrnd1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/1/13/Hirgrnd1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hirgrnd1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Seizo Yamada's ground level photo taken approximately 7 km (4.3 mi) northeast of Hiroshima</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hiroshima_10km.jpg"><img alt="Another view of the mushroom cloud forming, from further away." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="857" data-file-width="610" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Hiroshima_10km.jpg/170px-Hiroshima_10km.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Hiroshima_10km.jpg/255px-Hiroshima_10km.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Hiroshima_10km.jpg/340px-Hiroshima_10km.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hiroshima_10km.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Picture found in Honkawa Elementary School in 2013 of the Hiroshima atom bomb cloud, stated by some books and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hiroshima_Peace_Museum" title="Hiroshima Peace Museum">Hiroshima Peace Museum</a> as having been taken about 30 minutes after detonation from about 10 km (6.2 mi) east of the hypocenter. However, experience on how quickly such clouds dissipate and comparisons to other photos puts this frame at 2-3 minutes after detonation, not 30 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hiroshima was the primary target of the first nuclear bombing mission on August 6, with Kokura and Nagasaki as alternative targets. Having been fully briefed under the terms of <a href="/wiki/Operations_Order_No._35" title="Operations Order No. 35">Operations Order No. 35</a>, the 393d Bombardment Squadron B-29 <i><a href="/wiki/Enola_Gay" title="Enola Gay">Enola Gay</a></i>, piloted by Tibbets, took off from North Field, <a href="/wiki/Tinian" title="Tinian">Tinian</a>, about six hours' flight time from Japan. The <i>Enola Gay</i> (named after Tibbets' mother) was accompanied by two other B-29s. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Artiste" title="The Great Artiste">The Great Artiste</a></i>, commanded by Major <a href="/wiki/Charles_Sweeney" title="Charles Sweeney">Charles Sweeney</a>, carried instrumentation, and a then-nameless aircraft later called <i><a href="/wiki/Necessary_Evil_(aircraft)" title="Necessary Evil (aircraft)">Necessary Evil</a></i>, commanded by Captain George Marquardt, served as the photography aircraft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-509timeline_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-509timeline-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto; float:none;">

<td>Strike observation and photography</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Top_Secret_(B-29)" title="Top Secret (B-29)">Top Secret</a></i></td>
<td>Captain Charles F. McKnight</td>
<td>Dimples 72</td>
<td>Strike spare—did not complete mission</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>After leaving Tinian the aircraft made their way separately to Iwo Jima to rendezvous with Sweeney and Marquardt at 05:55 at 9,200 feet (2,800 m),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDietzVan_Kirk2012462_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDietzVan_Kirk2012462-128">[128]</a></sup> and set course for Japan. The aircraft arrived over the target in clear visibility at 31,060 feet (9,470 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDietzVan_Kirk2012467_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDietzVan_Kirk2012467-129">[129]</a></sup> Parsons, who was in command of the mission, armed the bomb during the flight to minimize the risks during takeoff. He had witnessed four B-29s crash and burn at takeoff, and feared that a nuclear explosion would occur if a B-29 crashed with an armed Little Boy on board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisTolzer195772_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisTolzer195772-130">[130]</a></sup> His assistant, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Lieutenant" title="Second Lieutenant">Second Lieutenant</a> <a href="/wiki/Morris_R._Jeppson" title="Morris R. Jeppson">Morris R. Jeppson</a>, removed the safety devices 30 minutes before reaching the target area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the night of August 5–6, Japanese early warning radar detected the approach of numerous American aircraft headed for the southern part of Japan. Radar detected 65 bombers headed for Saga, 102 bound for <a href="/wiki/Maebashi" title="Maebashi">Maebashi</a>, 261 en route to <a href="/wiki/Nishinomiya" title="Nishinomiya">Nishinomiya</a>, 111 headed for <a href="/wiki/Ube,_Yamaguchi" title="Ube, Yamaguchi">Ube</a> and 66 bound for Imabari. An alert was given and radio broadcasting stopped in many cities, among them Hiroshima. The all-clear was sounded in Hiroshima at 00:05.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977391.E2.80.93392_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977391.E2.80.93392-132">[132]</a></sup> About an hour before the bombing, the air raid alert was sounded again, as <i>Straight Flush</i> flew over the city. It broadcast a short message which was picked up by <i>Enola Gay</i>. It read: "Cloud cover less than 3/10th at all altitudes. Advice: bomb primary."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977414_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977414-133">[133]</a></sup> The all-clear was sounded over Hiroshima again at 07:09.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977415_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977415-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>At 08:09, Tibbets started his bomb run and handed control over to his bombardier, Major <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Ferebee" title="Thomas Ferebee">Thomas Ferebee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen19692566_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen19692566-135">[135]</a></sup> The release at 08:15 (Hiroshima time) went as planned, and the Little Boy containing about 64 kg (141 lb) of uranium-235 took 44.4 seconds to fall from the aircraft flying at about 31,000 feet (9,400 m) to a detonation height of about 1,900 feet (580 m) above the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKerr_et_al200542.E2.80.9343_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKerr_et_al200542.E2.80.9343-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malik_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Malik-137">[137]</a></sup> <i>Enola Gay</i> traveled 11.5 mi (18.5 km) before it felt the shock waves from the blast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Firestorm_cloud_over_Hiroshima,_near_local_noon._Aug_6_1945.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="717" data-file-width="887" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Firestorm_cloud_over_Hiroshima%2C_near_local_noon._Aug_6_1945.jpg/220px-Firestorm_cloud_over_Hiroshima%2C_near_local_noon._Aug_6_1945.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Firestorm_cloud_over_Hiroshima%2C_near_local_noon._Aug_6_1945.jpg/330px-Firestorm_cloud_over_Hiroshima%2C_near_local_noon._Aug_6_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Firestorm_cloud_over_Hiroshima%2C_near_local_noon._Aug_6_1945.jpg/440px-Firestorm_cloud_over_Hiroshima%2C_near_local_noon._Aug_6_1945.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Firestorm_cloud_over_Hiroshima,_near_local_noon._Aug_6_1945.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
For decades this "Hiroshima strike" photo was misidentified as the <a href="/wiki/Mushroom_cloud" title="Mushroom cloud">mushroom cloud</a> of the bomb that formed at c. 08:16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Hiroshima_Mushroom_Cloud_That_Wasn.27t_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Hiroshima_Mushroom_Cloud_That_Wasn.27t-140">[140]</a></sup> However, due to its much greater height, the scene was identified by a researcher in March 2016 as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyrocumulonimbus_cloud" title="Pyrocumulonimbus cloud">firestorm-cloud</a> that engulfed the city,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Hiroshima_Mushroom_Cloud_That_Wasn.27t_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Hiroshima_Mushroom_Cloud_That_Wasn.27t-140">[140]</a></sup> a fire that reached its peak intensity some three hours after the bomb.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atmospheric_effects_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Atmospheric_effects-141">[141]</a></sup> The image with the incorrect description featured prominently in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hiroshima_Peace_Museum" title="Hiroshima Peace Museum">Hiroshima Peace Museum</a> up to 2016,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Hiroshima_Mushroom_Cloud_That_Wasn.27t_140-2"><a href="#cite_note-The_Hiroshima_Mushroom_Cloud_That_Wasn.27t-140">[140]</a></sup> though not cited, it had much earlier, also been mis-attributed and presented to the public in 1955 by US artists, with the world-touring <i><a href="/wiki/The_Family_of_Man" title="The Family of Man">The Family of Man</a></i> exhibition. Without knowledge of the photo the output of energy from the fuel in the city, necessary to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cloud_formation" title="Cloud formation">loft</a> a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stratospheric" title="Stratospheric">stratospheric</a> firestorm-cloud, had been estimated as 1000 times the energy of the bomb.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atmospheric_effects_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-Atmospheric_effects-141">[141]</a></sup> Post March estimates using the height of this Hiroshima-cloud also point at the underlying <a href="/wiki/Firestorm" title="Firestorm">firestorm</a> releasing approximately 1000 times the energy of the bomb.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Hiroshima_Mushroom_Cloud_That_Wasn.27t_140-3"><a href="#cite_note-The_Hiroshima_Mushroom_Cloud_That_Wasn.27t-140">[140]</a></sup> Twenty minutes after detonation, during the formation of this firestorm, soot filled <a href="/wiki/Black_Rain_(novel)" title="Black Rain (novel)">black rain</a> began to fall on survivors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Scientist <a href="/wiki/Alan_Robock" title="Alan Robock">Alan Robock</a> suggests that 100 of these firestorm-clouds would create a <i>small</i> "<a href="/wiki/Nuclear_winter" title="Nuclear winter">nuclear winter</a>", 1-2 C of global cooling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Due to <a href="/wiki/Crosswind" title="Crosswind">crosswind</a>, the bomb missed the <a href="/wiki/Aiming_point" title="Aiming point">aiming point</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Aioi_Bridge" title="Aioi Bridge">Aioi Bridge</a>, by approximately 800 ft (240 m) and detonated directly over <a href="/wiki/Shima_Hospital" title="Shima Hospital">Shima Surgical Clinic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977423._427_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977423._427-144">[144]</a></sup> at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki&amp;params=34.39468_N_132.45462_E_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">34°23′41″N</span> <span class="longitude">132°27′17″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">34.39468°N 132.45462°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">34.39468; 132.45462</span></span></span></a></span>. It released the equivalent energy of 16 <a href="/wiki/TNT_equivalent" title="TNT equivalent">kilotons of TNT</a> (67 TJ), ± 2 kt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKerr_et_al200542.E2.80.9343_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKerr_et_al200542.E2.80.9343-136">[136]</a></sup> The weapon was <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon_design#Gun-type_assembly_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon design">considered very inefficient</a>, with only 1.7% of its material fissioning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cotmplitboy_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-cotmplitboy-145">[145]</a></sup> The radius of total destruction was about 1 mile (1.6 km), with resulting fires across 4.4 square miles (11 km<sup>2</sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_DNATR805512F_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org_DNATR805512F-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>People on the ground reported seeing a <i>pika</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span lang="ja">ピカ</span>)</span>—a brilliant flash of light—followed by a <i>don</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span lang="ja">ドン</span>)</span>—a loud booming sound.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrank1999264.E2.80.93265_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrank1999264.E2.80.93265-147">[147]</a></sup> Some 70,000–80,000 people, or around 30% of the population of Hiroshima, were killed by the blast and resultant firestorm,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> and another 70,000 injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> Perhaps as many as 20,000 Japanese military personnel were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrank1999286.E2.80.9387_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrank1999286.E2.80.9387-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Enola Gay</i> stayed over the target area for two minutes and was ten miles away when the bomb detonated. Only Tibbets, Parsons, and Ferebee knew of the nature of the weapon; the others on the bomber were only told to expect a blinding flash and given black goggles. "It was hard to believe what we saw", Tibbets told reporters, while Parsons said "the whole thing was tremendous and awe-inspiring ... the men aboard with me gasped 'My God'". He and Tibbets compared the shockwave to "a close burst of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ack-ack" title="Ack-ack">ack-ack</a> fire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian19450808_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian19450808-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events_on_the_ground">Events on the ground</span></h3>
<p>Some of the reinforced concrete buildings in Hiroshima had been very strongly constructed because of the earthquake danger in Japan, and their framework did not collapse even though they were fairly close to the blast center. Since the bomb detonated in the air, the blast was directed more downward than sideways, which was largely responsible for the survival of the <i><a href="/wiki/Hiroshima_Peace_Memorial" title="Hiroshima Peace Memorial">Prefectural Industrial Promotional Hall</a></i>, now commonly known as the <i>Genbaku</i> (A-bomb) dome. This building was designed and built by the Czech architect <a href="/wiki/Jan_Letzel" title="Jan Letzel">Jan Letzel</a>, and was only 150 m (490 ft) from ground zero. The ruin was named <i>Hiroshima Peace Memorial</i> and was made a UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in 1996 over the objections of the United States and China, which expressed reservations on the grounds that other Asian nations were the ones who suffered the greatest loss of life and property, and a focus on Japan lacked historical perspective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>The US surveys estimated that 4.7 square miles (12 km<sup>2</sup>) of the city were destroyed. Japanese officials determined that 69% of Hiroshima's buildings were destroyed and another 6–7% damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-154">[154]</a></sup> The bombing started fires that spread rapidly through timber and paper homes. As in other Japanese cities, the firebreaks proved ineffective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHam2011330_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHam2011330-155">[155]</a></sup></p>

<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Agnew_StrikeOrderHiroshima.jpg" title="Strike order for the Hiroshima bombing as posted on August 5, 1945"><img alt="A typed page of instructions" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="965" data-file-width="620" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Agnew_StrikeOrderHiroshima.jpg/128px-Agnew_StrikeOrderHiroshima.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Agnew_StrikeOrderHiroshima.jpg/193px-Agnew_StrikeOrderHiroshima.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Agnew_StrikeOrderHiroshima.jpg/257px-Agnew_StrikeOrderHiroshima.jpg 2x" width="128"/></a></div>

</tr>

<p>Eizō Nomura was the closest known survivor, who was in the basement of a reinforced concrete building (it remained as the <i><a href="/wiki/Hiroshima_Peace_Memorial_Park#Rest_House" title="Hiroshima Peace Memorial Park">Rest House</a></i> after the war) only 170 metres (560 ft) from <a href="/wiki/Ground_zero" title="Ground zero">ground zero</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Hypocenter" title="Hypocenter">hypocenter</a>) at the time of the attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> He lived into his 80s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Akiko Takakura was among the closest survivors to the hypocenter of the blast. She had been in the solidly built Bank of Hiroshima only 300 meters (980 ft) from ground-zero at the time of the attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over 90% of the doctors and 93% of the nurses in Hiroshima were killed or injured—most had been in the downtown area which received the greatest damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> The hospitals were destroyed or heavily damaged. Only one doctor, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Terufumi_Sasaki&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Terufumi Sasaki (page does not exist)">Terufumi Sasaki</a>, remained on duty at the Red Cross Hospital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHam2011330_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHam2011330-155">[155]</a></sup> Nonetheless, by early afternoon, the police and volunteers had established evacuation centres at hospitals, schools and tram stations, and a morgue was established in the Asano library.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHam2011330.E2.80.93331_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHam2011330.E2.80.93331-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most elements of the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Second_General_Army_(Japan)" title="Second General Army (Japan)">Second General Army</a> headquarters were at physical training on the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima_Castle" title="Hiroshima Castle">Hiroshima Castle</a>, barely 900 yards (820 m) from the hypocenter. The attack killed 3,243 troops on the parade ground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHam2011325_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHam2011325-163">[163]</a></sup> The communications room of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chugoku_Military_District_Headquarters&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chugoku Military District Headquarters (page does not exist)">Chugoku Military District Headquarters</a> that was responsible for issuing and lifting air raid warnings was in a semi-basement in the castle. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Yoshie_Oka&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Yoshie Oka (page does not exist)">Yoshie Oka</a>, a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hijiyama_Girls_High_School&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hijiyama Girls High School (page does not exist)">Hijiyama Girls High School</a> student who had been <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conscript" title="Conscript">conscripted</a>/mobilized to serve as a communications officer had just sent a message that the alarm had been issued for Hiroshima and neighboring <a href="/wiki/Yamaguchi,_Yamaguchi" title="Yamaguchi, Yamaguchi">Yamaguchi</a>, when the bomb exploded. She used a special phone to inform<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (December 2016)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Fukuyama,_Hiroshima" title="Fukuyama, Hiroshima">Fukuyama</a> Headquarters (some 100 km away) that "Hiroshima has been attacked by a new type of bomb. The city is in a state of near-total destruction."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since Mayor <a href="/wiki/Senkichi_Awaya" title="Senkichi Awaya">Senkichi Awaya</a> had been killed while eating breakfast with his son and granddaughter at the mayoral residence, Field Marshal <a href="/wiki/Shunroku_Hata" title="Shunroku Hata">Hata</a>, who was only slightly wounded, took over the administration of the city, and coordinated relief efforts. Many of his staff had been killed or fatally wounded, including a Korean prince of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseon_Dynasty" title="Joseon Dynasty">Joseon Dynasty</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_Wu" title="Yi Wu">Yi Wu</a>, who was serving as a lieutenant colonel in the Japanese Army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977443.E2.80.93444_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977443.E2.80.93444-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Hata's senior surviving staff officer was the wounded Colonel <a href="/wiki/Kumao_Imoto" title="Kumao Imoto">Kumao Imoto</a>, who acted as his chief of staff. Soldiers from the undamaged Hiroshima Ujina Harbor used <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shinyo-class_suicide_motorboat" title="Shinyo-class suicide motorboat">suicide boats</a>, intended to repel the American invasion, to collect the wounded and take them down the rivers to the military hospital at <a href="/wiki/Ujina" title="Ujina">Ujina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977443-444_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977443-444-167">[167]</a></sup> Trucks and trains brought in relief supplies and evacuated survivors from the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHam2011333_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHam2011333-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>Twelve American airmen were imprisoned at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chugoku_Military_Police_Headquarters&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chugoku Military Police Headquarters (page does not exist)">Chugoku Military Police Headquarters</a> located about 1,300 feet (400 m) from the hypocenter of the blast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> Most died instantly, although two were reported to have been executed by their captors, and two prisoners badly injured by the bombing were left next to the Aioi Bridge by the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kempei_Tai" title="Kempei Tai">Kempei Tai</a></i>, where they were stoned to death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977444.E2.80.93445_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977444.E2.80.93445-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> Eight U.S. prisoners of war killed as part of the medical experiments program at <a href="/wiki/Kyushu_University" title="Kyushu University">Kyushu University</a> were falsely reported by Japanese authorities as having been killed in the atomic blast as part of an attempted cover up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japanese_realization_of_the_bombing">Japanese realization of the bombing</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:415px;max-width:415px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:203px;max-width:203px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AtomicEffects-p7a.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="506" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/AtomicEffects-p7a.jpg/201px-AtomicEffects-p7a.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/AtomicEffects-p7a.jpg/302px-AtomicEffects-p7a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/AtomicEffects-p7a.jpg/402px-AtomicEffects-p7a.jpg 2x" width="201"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Hiroshima before the bombing</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:208px;max-width:208px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AtomicEffects-p7b.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="520" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/AtomicEffects-p7b.jpg/206px-AtomicEffects-p7b.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/AtomicEffects-p7b.jpg/309px-AtomicEffects-p7b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/AtomicEffects-p7b.jpg/412px-AtomicEffects-p7b.jpg 2x" width="206"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Hiroshima after the bombing and <a href="/wiki/Firestorm" title="Firestorm">firestorm</a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Tokyo control operator of the <a href="/wiki/NHK" title="NHK">Japan Broadcasting Corporation</a> noticed that the Hiroshima station had gone off the air. He tried to re-establish his program by using another telephone line, but it too had failed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-No_High_Ground_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-No_High_Ground-173">[173]</a></sup> About 20 minutes later the Tokyo railroad telegraph center realized that the main line telegraph had stopped working just north of Hiroshima. From some small railway stops within 16 km (10 mi) of the city came unofficial and confused reports of a terrible explosion in Hiroshima. All these reports were transmitted to the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army_General_Staff_Office" title="Imperial Japanese Army General Staff Office">Imperial Japanese Army General Staff</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Official_Report_on_the_Bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Report_on_the_Bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>Military bases repeatedly tried to call the Army Control Station in Hiroshima. The complete silence from that city puzzled the General Staff; they knew that no large enemy raid had occurred and that no sizable store of explosives was in Hiroshima at that time. A young officer was instructed to fly immediately to Hiroshima, to land, survey the damage, and return to Tokyo with reliable information for the staff. It was felt that nothing serious had taken place and that the explosion was just a rumor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Official_Report_on_the_Bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki_174-1"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Report_on_the_Bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>The staff officer went to the airport and took off for the southwest. After flying for about three hours, while still nearly 160 km (100 mi) from Hiroshima, he and his pilot saw a great cloud of smoke from the bomb. After circling the city in order to survey the damage they landed south of the city, where the staff officer, after reporting to Tokyo, began to organize relief measures. Tokyo's first indication that the city had been destroyed by a new type of bomb came from President Truman's announcement of the strike, sixteen hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Official_Report_on_the_Bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki_174-2"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Report_on_the_Bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="Events_of_August_7–9"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Events_of_August_7.E2.80.939">Events of August 7–9</span></h2>
<table class="mbox-small" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Audio-input-microphone.svg/50px-Audio-input-microphone.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Audio-input-microphone.svg/75px-Audio-input-microphone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Audio-input-microphone.svg/100px-Audio-input-microphone.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">

</table>
<p>After the Hiroshima bombing, Truman issued a statement announcing the use of the new weapon. He stated, "We may be grateful to Providence" that <a href="/wiki/German_nuclear_weapon_project" title="German nuclear weapon project">the German atomic bomb project</a> had failed, and that the United States and its allies had "spent two billion dollars on the greatest scientific gamble in history—and won". Truman then warned Japan: "If they do not now accept our terms, they may expect a rain of ruin from the air, the like of which has never been seen on this earth. Behind this air attack will follow sea and land forces in such numbers and power as they have not yet seen and with the fighting skill of which they are already well aware."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> This was a widely broadcast speech picked up by Japanese news agencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Agnew_Leaflet.jpg"><img alt="Brownish leaflet covered in Japanese writing" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1034" data-file-width="677" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Agnew_Leaflet.jpg/170px-Agnew_Leaflet.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Agnew_Leaflet.jpg/255px-Agnew_Leaflet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Agnew_Leaflet.jpg/340px-Agnew_Leaflet.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Agnew_Leaflet.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Leaflet AB12,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.psywarrior.com_OWI60YrsLater2_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.psywarrior.com_OWI60YrsLater2-177">[177]</a></sup> with information on the Hiroshima bomb and a warning to civilians to petition the Emperor to surrender was dropped over Japan beginning on August 9,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.psywarrior.com_OWI60YrsLater2_177-1"><a href="#cite_note-www.psywarrior.com_OWI60YrsLater2-177">[177]</a></sup> by the 509th Composite Group on the bombing mission. Although it is not identified by them, an AB11 is in the possession of the <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki_Atomic_Bomb_Museum" title="Nagasaki Atomic Bomb Museum">Nagasaki Atomic Bomb Museum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By August 8,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> the 50,000-watt <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AM_radio" title="AM radio">standard wave</a> station on <a href="/wiki/Saipan" title="Saipan">Saipan</a> the OWI <a href="/wiki/Radio_station" title="Radio station">radio station</a>, broadcast a similar message to Japan every 15 minutes about Hiroshima, stating that more Japanese cities would face a similar fate in the absence of immediate acceptance of the terms of the Potsdam Declaration and emphatically urged civilians to evacuate major cities. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_Japan" title="Radio Japan">Radio Japan</a>, which continued to extoll victory for Japan by never surrendering,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Information_War_in_the_Pacific_86-3"><a href="#cite_note-The_Information_War_in_the_Pacific-86">[86]</a></sup> had informed the Japanese of the destruction of Hiroshima by a single bomb.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prime Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suzuki_Kantar%C5%8D" title="Suzuki Kantarō">Suzuki</a> felt compelled to meet the Japanese press, to whom he reiterated his government's commitment to ignore the Allies' demands and fight on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> The Japanese government did not react. Emperor <a href="/wiki/Hirohito" title="Hirohito">Hirohito</a>, the government, and the war council considered four conditions for surrender: the preservation of the <i><a href="/wiki/Kokutai" title="Kokutai">kokutai</a></i> (Imperial institution and national <a href="/wiki/Polity" title="Polity">polity</a>), assumption by the Imperial Headquarters of responsibility for disarmament and demobilization, no occupation of the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_archipelago" title="Japanese archipelago">Japanese Home Islands</a>, Korea, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Formosa" title="Formosa">Formosa</a>, and delegation of the punishment of war criminals to the Japanese government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBix1996512_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBix1996512-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<p>Soviet Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Vyacheslav_Molotov" title="Vyacheslav Molotov">Vyacheslav Molotov</a> informed Tokyo of the Soviet Union's unilateral abrogation of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_Neutrality_Pact" title="Soviet–Japanese Neutrality Pact">Soviet–Japanese Neutrality Pact</a> on August 5. At two minutes past midnight on August 9, <a href="/wiki/Japan_Standard_Time" title="Japan Standard Time">Tokyo time</a>, Soviet infantry, armor, and air forces had launched the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchurian_Strategic_Offensive_Operation" title="Manchurian Strategic Offensive Operation">Manchurian Strategic Offensive Operation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESlavinski.C4.AD2004153.E2.80.93154_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESlavinski.C4.AD2004153.E2.80.93154-183">[183]</a></sup> Four hours later, word reached Tokyo of the Soviet Union's official declaration of war. The senior leadership of the Japanese Army began preparations to impose <a href="/wiki/Martial_law" title="Martial law">martial law</a> on the nation, with the support of Minister of War <a href="/wiki/Korechika_Anami" title="Korechika Anami">Korechika Anami</a>, in order to stop anyone attempting to make peace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrank1999288.E2.80.93289_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrank1999288.E2.80.93289-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 7, a day after Hiroshima was destroyed, Dr. <a href="/wiki/Yoshio_Nishina" title="Yoshio Nishina">Yoshio Nishina</a> and other atomic physicists arrived at the city, and carefully examined the damage. They then went back to Tokyo and told the cabinet that Hiroshima was indeed destroyed by an atomic bomb. Admiral <a href="/wiki/Soemu_Toyoda" title="Soemu Toyoda">Soemu Toyoda</a>, the Chief of the Naval General Staff, estimated that no more than one or two additional bombs could be readied, so they decided to endure the remaining attacks, acknowledging "there would be more destruction but the war would go on".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyt2001401_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyt2001401-185">[185]</a></sup> American <a href="/wiki/Magic_(cryptography)" title="Magic (cryptography)">Magic codebreakers</a> intercepted the cabinet's messages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrank1999283.E2.80.93284_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrank1999283.E2.80.93284-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<p>Purnell, Parsons, Tibbets, Spaatz, and LeMay met on Guam that same day to discuss what should be done next.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERuss199064.E2.80.9365_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERuss199064.E2.80.9365-187">[187]</a></sup> Since there was no indication of Japan surrendering,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrank1999283.E2.80.93284_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrank1999283.E2.80.93284-186">[186]</a></sup> they decided to proceed with dropping another bomb. Parsons said that Project Alberta would have it ready by August 11, but Tibbets pointed to weather reports indicating poor flying conditions on that day due to a storm, and asked if the bomb could be readied by August 9. Parsons agreed to try to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGroves1962342_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGroves1962342-188">[188]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERuss199064.E2.80.9365_187-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERuss199064.E2.80.9365-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nagasaki_during_World_War_II">Nagasaki during World War II</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bocks-Car-enlisted-flight-crew.png"><img alt="Formal picture of ten men in uniform. Five are standing and five are kneeling. In contrast to the Enola Gay picture, all are in correct uniform. The five standing are wearing ties, and all but one of the ten wears a peaked cap or garrison cap." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="624" data-file-width="714" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Bocks-Car-enlisted-flight-crew.png/220px-Bocks-Car-enlisted-flight-crew.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Bocks-Car-enlisted-flight-crew.png/330px-Bocks-Car-enlisted-flight-crew.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Bocks-Car-enlisted-flight-crew.png/440px-Bocks-Car-enlisted-flight-crew.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bocks-Car-enlisted-flight-crew.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i><a href="/wiki/Bockscar" title="Bockscar">Bockscar</a></i> and its crew, who dropped the <a href="/wiki/Fat_Man" title="Fat Man">Fat Man</a> atomic bomb on Nagasaki</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city of Nagasaki had been one of the largest seaports in southern Japan, and was of great wartime importance because of its wide-ranging industrial activity, including the production of <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ordnance" title="wikt:ordnance">ordnance</a>, ships, military equipment, and other war materials. The four largest companies in the city were <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi" title="Mitsubishi">Mitsubishi</a> Shipyards, Electrical Shipyards, Arms Plant, and Steel and Arms Works, which employed about 90% of the city's labor force, and accounted for 90% of the city's industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nagasaki_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nagasaki-189">[189]</a></sup> Although an important industrial city, Nagasaki had been spared from firebombing because its geography made it difficult to locate at night with <a href="/wiki/AN/APQ-13" title="AN/APQ-13">AN/APQ-13</a> radar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrank1999263_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrank1999263-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unlike the other target cities, Nagasaki had not been placed off limits to bombers by the Joint Chiefs of Staff's July 3 directive,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrank1999263_118-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrank1999263-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGroves1962309_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGroves1962309-190">[190]</a></sup> and was bombed on a small scale five times. During one of these raids on August 1, a number of conventional high-explosive bombs were dropped on the city. A few hit the shipyards and dock areas in the southwest portion of the city, and several hit the Mitsubishi Steel and Arms Works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nagasaki_189-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nagasaki-189">[189]</a></sup> By early August, the city was defended by the 134th Anti-Aircraft Regiment of the 4th Anti-Aircraft Division with four batteries of 7 cm (2.8 in) anti-aircraft guns and two <a href="/wiki/Searchlight" title="Searchlight">searchlight</a> batteries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZalogaNoon201059_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZalogaNoon201059-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>In contrast to Hiroshima, almost all of the buildings were of old-fashioned Japanese construction, consisting of timber or timber-framed buildings with timber walls (with or without plaster) and tile roofs. Many of the smaller industries and business establishments were also situated in buildings of timber or other materials not designed to withstand explosions. Nagasaki had been permitted to grow for many years without conforming to any definite city zoning plan; residences were erected adjacent to factory buildings and to each other almost as closely as possible throughout the entire industrial valley. On the day of the bombing, an estimated 263,000 people were in Nagasaki, including 240,000 Japanese residents, 10,000 Korean residents, 2,500 conscripted Korean workers, 9,000 Japanese soldiers, 600 conscripted Chinese workers, and 400 Allied prisoners of war in a camp to the north of Nagasaki.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977353.E2.80.93354_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomasMorgan-Witts1977353.E2.80.93354-192">[192]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bombing_of_Nagasaki">Bombing of Nagasaki</span></h3>
<p>Responsibility for the timing of the second bombing was delegated to Tibbets. Scheduled for August 11 against Kokura, the raid was moved earlier by two days to avoid a five-day period of bad weather forecast to begin on August 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESherwin2003233.E2.80.9323_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESherwin2003233.E2.80.9323-193">[193]</a></sup> Three bomb pre-assemblies had been transported to Tinian, labeled F-31, F-32, and F-33 on their exteriors. On August 8, a dress rehearsal was conducted off Tinian by Sweeney using <i><a href="/wiki/Bockscar" title="Bockscar">Bockscar</a></i> as the drop airplane. Assembly F-33 was expended testing the components and F-31 was designated for the August 9 mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECampbell2005114_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECampbell2005114-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto; float:none;">
<caption><b>Special Mission 16, Secondary target Nagasaki, August 9, 1945</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECampbell200532_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECampbell200532-195">[195]</a></sup></caption>
<tr style="background: olive">
